This client also interacts with the broker to allow groups of\n    57→ * consumers to load balance consumption using <a href=\"#consumergroups\">consumer groups</a>.\n    58→ * <p>\n    59→ * The consumer maintains TCP connections to the necessary brokers to fetch data.\n    60→ * Failure to close the consumer after use will leak these connections.\n    61→ * The consumer is not thread-safe. See <a href=\"#multithreaded\">Multi-threaded Processing</a> for more details.\n    62→ *\n    63→ * <h3>Cross-Version Compatibility</h3>\n    64→ * This client can communicate with brokers that are version 0.10.0 or newer. Older or newer brokers may not support\n    65→ * certain features. For example, 0.10.0 brokers do not support offsetsForTimes, because this feature was added\n    66→ * in version 0.10.1. You will receive an {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.UnsupportedVersionException}\n    67→ * when invoking an API that is not available on the running broker version.\n    68→ * <p>\n    69→ *\n    70→ * <h3>Offsets and Consumer Position</h3>\n    71→ * Kafka maintains a numerical offset for each record in a partition. This offset acts as a unique identifier of\n    72→ * a record within that partition, and also denotes the position of the consumer in the partition. For example, a consumer\n    73→ * which is at position 5 has consumed records with offsets 0 through 4 and will next receive the record with offset 5.\n    74→ * Note that offsets are not guaranteed to be consecutive (such as compacted topic or when records have been produced\n    75→ * using transactions). For example, if the consumer did read a record with offset 4, but 5 is not an offset\n    76→ * with a record, its position might advance to 6 (or higher) directly. Similarly, if the consumer's position is 5,\n    77→ * but there is no record with offset 5, the consumer will return the record with the next higher offset.\n    78→ * There are actually two notions of position relevant to the user of the consumer:\n    79→ * <p>\n    80→ * The {@link #position(TopicPartition) position} of the consumer gives the offset of the next record that will be given\n    81→ * out. It will be one larger than the highest offset the consumer has seen in that partition. It automatically advances\n    82→ * every time the consumer receives messages in a call to {@link #poll(Duration)}.\n    83→ * <p>\n    84→ * The {@link #commitSync() committed position} is the last offset that has been stored securely. Should the\n    85→ * process fail and restart, this is the offset that the consumer will recover to. The consumer can either automatically commit\n    86→ * offsets periodically; or it can choose to control this committed position manually by calling one of the commit APIs\n    87→ * (e.g. {@link #commitSync() commitSync} and {@link #commitAsync(OffsetCommitCallback) commitAsync}).\n    88→ * <p>\n    89→ * This distinction gives the consumer control over when a record is considered consumed. It is discussed in further\n    90→ * detail below.\n    91→ *\n    92→ * <h3><a name=\"consumergroups\">Consumer Groups and Topic Subscriptions</a></h3>\n    93→ *\n    94→ * Kafka uses the concept of <i>consumer groups</i> to allow a pool of processes to divide the work of consuming and\n    95→ * processing records. These processes can either be running on the same machine or they can be\n    96→ * distributed over many machines to provide scalability and fault tolerance for processing. All consumer instances\n    97→ * sharing the same {@code group.id} will be part of the same consumer group.\n    98→ * <p>\n    99→ * Each consumer in a group can dynamically set the list of topics it wants to subscribe to through one of the\n   100→ * {@link #subscribe(Collection, ConsumerRebalanceListener) subscribe} APIs. This offset acts as a unique identifier of\n * a record within that partition, and also denotes the position of the consumer in the partition. For example, a consumer\n * which is at position 5 has consumed records with offsets 0 through 4 and will next receive the record with offset 5.\n * Note that offsets are not guaranteed to be consecutive (such as compacted topic or when records have been produced\n * using transactions). For example, if the consumer did read a record with offset 4, but 5 is not an offset\n * with a record, its position might advance to 6 (or higher) directly. Similarly, if the consumer's position is 5,\n * but there is no record with offset 5, the consumer will return the record with the next higher offset.\n * There are actually two notions of position relevant to the user of the consumer:\n * <p>\n * The {@link #position(TopicPartition) position} of the consumer gives the offset of the next record that will be given\n * out. It will be one larger than the highest offset the consumer has seen in that partition. It automatically advances\n * every time the consumer receives messages in a call to {@link #poll(Duration)}.\n * <p>\n * The {@link #commitSync() committed position} is the last offset that has been stored securely. Should the\n * process fail and restart, this is the offset that the consumer will recover to. The consumer can either automatically commit\n * offsets periodically; or it can choose to control this committed position manually by calling one of the commit APIs\n * (e.g. {@link #commitSync() commitSync} and {@link #commitAsync(OffsetCommitCallback) commitAsync}).\n * <p>\n * This distinction gives the consumer control over when a record is considered consumed. It is discussed in further\n * detail below.\n *\n * <h3><a name=\"consumergroups\">Consumer Groups and Topic Subscriptions</a></h3>\n *\n * Kafka uses the concept of <i>consumer groups</i> to allow a pool of processes to divide the work of consuming and\n * processing records. These processes can either be running on the same machine or they can be\n * distributed over many machines to provide scalability and fault tolerance for processing. All consumer instances\n * sharing the same {@code group.id} will be part of the same consumer group.\n * <p>\n * Each consumer in a group can dynamically set the list of topics it wants to subscribe to through one of the\n * {@link #subscribe(Collection, ConsumerRebalanceListener) subscribe} APIs. Kafka will deliver each message in the","numLines":100,"startLine":1,"totalLines":1871}}}

This can be useful (for example) to store information about which\n * node made the commit, what time the commit was made, etc.\n */\npublic class OffsetAndMetadata implements Serializable {\n    private static final long serialVersionUID = 2019555404968089681L;\n\n    private final long offset;\n    private final String metadata;\n\n    // We use null to represent the absence of a leader epoch to simplify serialization.\n    // I.e., older serializations of this class which do not have this field will automatically\n    // initialize its value to null.\n    private final Integer leaderEpoch;\n\n    /**\n     * Construct a new OffsetAndMetadata object for committing through {@link KafkaConsumer}.\n     *\n     * @param offset The offset to be committed\n     * @param leaderEpoch Optional leader epoch of the last consumed record\n     * @param metadata Non-null metadata\n     */\n    public OffsetAndMetadata(long offset, Optional<Integer> leaderEpoch, String metadata) {\n        if (offset < 0)\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Invalid negative offset\");\n\n        this.offset = offset;\n        this.leaderEpoch = leaderEpoch.orElse(null);\n\n        // The server converts null metadata to an empty string. Analysis\\n\\n## Overview\\n\\nThe analysis examined the migration from the legacy Kafka ConsumerConnector API to the modern KafkaConsumer API in Apache Kafka. The current codebase (apache/kafka at commit 0753c489) implements the new KafkaConsumer API as the primary consumer interface.\\n\\n## Key Implementation Files\\n\\n### New KafkaConsumer API (New Implementation)\\n\\n**Main API Classes:**\\n- `KafkaConsumer` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java): The primary public consumer API implementing the Consumer interface. Provides poll-based consumption model with subscription or manual assignment.\\n- `Consumer` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/Consumer.java): Interface defining the consumer contract with methods for subscription, polling, and offset management.\\n\\n### Internal Implementation Architecture\\n\\nThe current KafkaConsumer uses a delegated architecture with two internal implementations:\\n\\n1. **AsyncKafkaConsumer** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java): Implements the new consumer group protocol (KIP-848) with event-driven architecture. Both the class and methods like `close(Duration)` are marked as @Deprecated, indicating transition to newer approaches.\\n\\n2. **ClassicKafkaConsumer** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java): Implements the legacy consumer group protocol. Also marked as @Deprecated, similar to AsyncKafkaConsumer.\\n\\n**Delegation Logic:**\\n- `ConsumerDelegateCreator` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegateCreator.java): Factory that selects between AsyncKafkaConsumer and ClassicKafkaConsumer based on the group protocol configuration. If `group.protocol` is set to \\\"consumer\\\", it uses AsyncKafkaConsumer; otherwise ClassicKafkaConsumer.\\n- `ConsumerDelegate` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegate.java): Interface that both implementations implement to provide a common abstraction.\\n\\n## Offset Management Key Differences\\n\\n### 1. **Offset Representation**\\n\\n**New API (KafkaConsumer):**\\n- Uses `OffsetAndMetadata` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/OffsetAndMetadata.java) to represent offsets\\n- Includes:\\n  - `offset`: The committed offset value\\n  - `metadata`: Optional application metadata (String)\\n  - `leaderEpoch`: Optional leader epoch for log truncation detection\\n- Constructor: `OffsetAndMetadata(long offset, Optional<Integer> leaderEpoch, String metadata)`\\n\\n### 2. **Position Tracking**\\n\\n**New API:**\\n- Uses `SubscriptionState` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/SubscriptionState.java) for tracking:\\n  - Assigned partitions (either via subscription or manual assignment)\\n  - Current position: The offset of the next record to be returned\\n  - Committed position: The last securely stored offset\\n  - Pause state for individual partitions\\n\\n### 3. **Offset Commit Management**\\n\\n**New API Methods:**\\n- `commitSync()`: Synchronously commits current position for all assigned partitions\\n- `commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> offsets)`: Explicitly commit specific offsets per partition\\n- `commitSync(Map, Duration timeout)`: With timeout specification\\n- `commitAsync()`: Asynchronously commit with optional callback\\n- `commitAsync(OffsetCommitCallback callback)`: With callback for success/failure\\n- `commitAsync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> offsets, OffsetCommitCallback callback)`: Async explicit offsets\\n\\n**Processing:** Handled by `CommitRequestManager` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CommitRequestManager.java) which:\\n- Manages pending offset commit requests\\n- Handles auto-commits based on `enable.auto.commit` and `auto.commit.interval.ms` configs\\n- Supports both synchronous and asynchronous commit models\\n- Provides callback invocation via `OffsetCommitCallbackInvoker`\\n- Handles failures with `CommitFailedException` and `RetriableCommitFailedException`\\n- Tracks member epoch for group coordination\\n\\n### 4. **Offset Fetching and Position Reset**\\n\\n**New API:**\\n- `OffsetFetcher` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/OffsetFetcher.java):\\n  - Fetches offsets for a given set of TopicPartition pairs\\n  - Handles offset reset strategies via `resetOffsets()`\\n  - Supports `offsetsForTimes()` to find offsets by timestamp\\n  - Manages leader epoch information for offset validation\\n  - Handles log truncation detection\\n\\n- `seek()` Methods:\\n  - `seek(TopicPartition partition, long offset)`: Seek to specific offset\\n  - `seek(TopicPartition partition, OffsetAndMetadata offsetAndMetadata)`: Seek with metadata\\n\\n### 5. **Committed Offset Retrieval**\\n\\n**New API:**\\n- `committed(Set<TopicPartition> partitions)`: Get last committed offset for partitions\\n- `committed(Set<TopicPartition> partitions, Duration timeout)`: With timeout\\n- Returns `Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>` for requested partitions\\n\\n### 6. **Position Query**\\n\\n**New API:**\\n- `position(TopicPartition partition)`: Returns long offset of next record to be returned\\n- `position(TopicPartition partition, Duration timeout)`: With timeout\\n\\n## Integration Examples\\n\\n### Camel Kafka Integration\\n\\nApache Camel (components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/) demonstrates the new API usage:\\n\\n1. **Factory Usage** (DefaultKafkaClientFactory.java):\\n   - Creates instances of `org.apache.kafka.clients.consumer.KafkaConsumer` directly\\n   - Passes configuration properties to the constructor\\n\\n2. **Offset Tracking** (KafkaFetchRecords.java, line 468-469):\\n   - Calls `consumer.committed(this.consumer.assignment())` to retrieve committed offsets\\n   - Iterates through TopicPartition->OffsetAndMetadata mappings\\n   - Uses `OffsetAndMetadata` objects for offset state\\n\\n## Key Behavioral Differences: Old vs New API\\n\\n### Automatic vs Manual Control\\n\\n**Legacy ConsumerConnector (Removed):**\\n- Provided implicit offset management\\n- Partitions were often managed automatically\\n- Limited control over commit timing\\n\\n**New KafkaConsumer API:**\\n- Explicit offset management via `commitSync()` and `commitAsync()`\\n- Clear separation between position (current offset) and committed (stored) offset\\n- Fine-grained control via `OffsetAndMetadata` including metadata and leader epoch\\n- Support for both automatic (`enable.auto.commit`) and manual commit modes\\n\\n### Error Handling\\n\\n**New API:**\\n- `CommitFailedException`: Thrown from `commitSync()` when commit fails non-retriably\\n- `RetriableCommitFailedException`: For transient failures allowing retry\\n- `NoOffsetForPartitionException`: When no offset reset strategy is configured\\n- Clear exception hierarchy for different failure scenarios\\n\\n### Metrics and Monitoring\\n\\n**New API:**\\n- `KafkaConsumerMetrics` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/metrics/KafkaConsumerMetrics.java)\\n- Provides detailed metrics for:\\n  - Consumer lag\\n  - Fetch rates and latencies\\n  - Commit success/failure rates\\n  - Rebalance timing and frequency\\n\\n## Conclusion\\n\\nThe migration from the legacy ConsumerConnector to the modern KafkaConsumer API represents a shift toward:\\n1. **Explicit offset management** using `OffsetAndMetadata` objects with metadata support\\n2. **Clear position semantics** distinguishing between current position and committed offset\\n3. **Flexible commit strategies** supporting both sync and async with callbacks\\n4. **Better error handling** with specific exception types for different failure modes\\n5. **Improved observability** through comprehensive metrics and leader epoch tracking\\n6. **Modern protocol support** with both legacy and new consumer group protocols available via delegation\\n\\nDownstream projects like Apache Camel have successfully migrated to use the new `KafkaConsumer` API, leveraging its explicit offset management and improved control mechanisms.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":925,"cache_read_input_tokens":69104,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":925},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"c831d8b8-2720-4d03-98da-709613b3c28c","uuid":"ae820796-c70f-4d3f-8ae3-ff003a76b7b0"}

Analysis\\n\\n## Overview\\n\\nThe analysis examined the migration from the legacy Kafka ConsumerConnector API to the modern KafkaConsumer API in Apache Kafka. The current codebase (apache/kafka at commit 0753c489) implements the new KafkaConsumer API as the primary consumer interface.\\n\\n## Key Implementation Files\\n\\n### New KafkaConsumer API (New Implementation)\\n\\n**Main API Classes:**\\n- `KafkaConsumer` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java): The primary public consumer API implementing the Consumer interface. Provides poll-based consumption model with subscription or manual assignment.\\n- `Consumer` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/Consumer.java): Interface defining the consumer contract with methods for subscription, polling, and offset management.\\n\\n### Internal Implementation Architecture\\n\\nThe current KafkaConsumer uses a delegated architecture with two internal implementations:\\n\\n1. **AsyncKafkaConsumer** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java): Implements the new consumer group protocol (KIP-848) with event-driven architecture. Both the class and methods like `close(Duration)` are marked as @Deprecated, indicating transition to newer approaches.\\n\\n2. **ClassicKafkaConsumer** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java): Implements the legacy consumer group protocol. Also marked as @Deprecated, similar to AsyncKafkaConsumer.\\n\\n**Delegation Logic:**\\n- `ConsumerDelegateCreator` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegateCreator.java): Factory that selects between AsyncKafkaConsumer and ClassicKafkaConsumer based on the group protocol configuration. If `group.protocol` is set to \\\"consumer\\\", it uses AsyncKafkaConsumer; otherwise ClassicKafkaConsumer.\\n- `ConsumerDelegate` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegate.java): Interface that both implementations implement to provide a common abstraction.\\n\\n## Offset Management Key Differences\\n\\n### 1. **Offset Representation**\\n\\n**New API (KafkaConsumer):**\\n- Uses `OffsetAndMetadata` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/OffsetAndMetadata.java) to represent offsets\\n- Includes:\\n  - `offset`: The committed offset value\\n  - `metadata`: Optional application metadata (String)\\n  - `leaderEpoch`: Optional leader epoch for log truncation detection\\n- Constructor: `OffsetAndMetadata(long offset, Optional<Integer> leaderEpoch, String metadata)`\\n\\n### 2. **Position Tracking**\\n\\n**New API:**\\n- Uses `SubscriptionState` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/SubscriptionState.java) for tracking:\\n  - Assigned partitions (either via subscription or manual assignment)\\n  - Current position: The offset of the next record to be returned\\n  - Committed position: The last securely stored offset\\n  - Pause state for individual partitions\\n\\n### 3. **Offset Commit Management**\\n\\n**New API Methods:**\\n- `commitSync()`: Synchronously commits current position for all assigned partitions\\n- `commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> offsets)`: Explicitly commit specific offsets per partition\\n- `commitSync(Map, Duration timeout)`: With timeout specification\\n- `commitAsync()`: Asynchronously commit with optional callback\\n- `commitAsync(OffsetCommitCallback callback)`: With callback for success/failure\\n- `commitAsync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> offsets, OffsetCommitCallback callback)`: Async explicit offsets\\n\\n**Processing:** Handled by `CommitRequestManager` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CommitRequestManager.java) which:\\n- Manages pending offset commit requests\\n- Handles auto-commits based on `enable.auto.commit` and `auto.commit.interval.ms` configs\\n- Supports both synchronous and asynchronous commit models\\n- Provides callback invocation via `OffsetCommitCallbackInvoker`\\n- Handles failures with `CommitFailedException` and `RetriableCommitFailedException`\\n- Tracks member epoch for group coordination\\n\\n### 4. **Offset Fetching and Position Reset**\\n\\n**New API:**\\n- `OffsetFetcher` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/OffsetFetcher.java):\\n  - Fetches offsets for a given set of TopicPartition pairs\\n  - Handles offset reset strategies via `resetOffsets()`\\n  - Supports `offsetsForTimes()` to find offsets by timestamp\\n  - Manages leader epoch information for offset validation\\n  - Handles log truncation detection\\n\\n- `seek()` Methods:\\n  - `seek(TopicPartition partition, long offset)`: Seek to specific offset\\n  - `seek(TopicPartition partition, OffsetAndMetadata offsetAndMetadata)`: Seek with metadata\\n\\n### 5. **Committed Offset Retrieval**\\n\\n**New API:**\\n- `committed(Set<TopicPartition> partitions)`: Get last committed offset for partitions\\n- `committed(Set<TopicPartition> partitions, Duration timeout)`: With timeout\\n- Returns `Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>` for requested partitions\\n\\n### 6. **Position Query**\\n\\n**New API:**\\n- `position(TopicPartition partition)`: Returns long offset of next record to be returned\\n- `position(TopicPartition partition, Duration timeout)`: With timeout\\n\\n## Integration Examples\\n\\n### Camel Kafka Integration\\n\\nApache Camel (components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/) demonstrates the new API usage:\\n\\n1. **Factory Usage** (DefaultKafkaClientFactory.java):\\n   - Creates instances of `org.apache.kafka.clients.consumer.KafkaConsumer` directly\\n   - Passes configuration properties to the constructor\\n\\n2. **Offset Tracking** (KafkaFetchRecords.java, line 468-469):\\n   - Calls `consumer.committed(this.consumer.assignment())` to retrieve committed offsets\\n   - Iterates through TopicPartition->OffsetAndMetadata mappings\\n   - Uses `OffsetAndMetadata` objects for offset state\\n\\n## Key Behavioral Differences: Old vs New API\\n\\n### Automatic vs Manual Control\\n\\n**Legacy ConsumerConnector (Removed):**\\n- Provided implicit offset management\\n- Partitions were often managed automatically\\n- Limited control over commit timing\\n\\n**New KafkaConsumer API:**\\n- Explicit offset management via `commitSync()` and `commitAsync()`\\n- Clear separation between position (current offset) and committed (stored) offset\\n- Fine-grained control via `OffsetAndMetadata` including metadata and leader epoch\\n- Support for both automatic (`enable.auto.commit`) and manual commit modes\\n\\n### Error Handling\\n\\n**New API:**\\n- `CommitFailedException`: Thrown from `commitSync()` when commit fails non-retriably\\n- `RetriableCommitFailedException`: For transient failures allowing retry\\n- `NoOffsetForPartitionException`: When no offset reset strategy is configured\\n- Clear exception hierarchy for different failure scenarios\\n\\n### Metrics and Monitoring\\n\\n**New API:**\\n- `KafkaConsumerMetrics` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/metrics/KafkaConsumerMetrics.java)\\n- Provides detailed metrics for:\\n  - Consumer lag\\n  - Fetch rates and latencies\\n  - Commit success/failure rates\\n  - Rebalance timing and frequency\\n\\n## Conclusion\\n\\nThe migration from the legacy ConsumerConnector to the modern KafkaConsumer API represents a shift toward:\\n1. **Explicit offset management** using `OffsetAndMetadata` objects with metadata support\\n2. **Clear position semantics** distinguishing between current position and committed offset\\n3. **Flexible commit strategies** supporting both sync and async with callbacks\\n4. **Better error handling** with specific exception types for different failure modes\\n5. **Improved observability** through comprehensive metrics and leader epoch tracking\\n6. **Modern protocol support** with both legacy and new consumer group protocols available via delegation\\n\\nDownstream projects like Apache Camel have successfully migrated to use the new `KafkaConsumer` API, leveraging its explicit offset management and improved control mechanisms.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
